        function gptClean(gptText) {
            if (typeof (gptText) == "string") {
                gptText = gptText.replace(/\&/g, '%26');
                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send
            .setTargeting('doi', gptClean('10.1002/smll.202302200')) // Publication DOI
            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

        googletag.defineSlot($GooglePublisherCategory, 'fluid', 'advert-leaderboard')

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="97da13e4b5cf47a3a66955264d59a99c">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'a391e091-d081-4add-9567-93e445a98f0e'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = '94C17C38B3BE414E516763881A95948E';
                var url = ('https:' == document.location.protocol ? 'https://' : 'http://')
                    + "beacon.riskified.com?shop=" + store_domain + "&sid=" + session_id;
                var s = document.createElement('script');
                s.type = 'text/javascript';
                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }
            if (window.attachEvent)
                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else
                window.addEventListener('load', riskifiedBeaconLoad, false);
        })();

aria-hidden="true" class="icon-related-circles-extend-button"></i><h2>Related</h2></a></li><li role="presentation" class="tab__nav__item"><a id="pane-pcw-detailscon-cloned" href="#pane-pcw-details" data-slide-clone="self" aria-controls="pane-pcw-details" role="menuitem" data-slide-target="#pane-pcw-details" class="tab__nav__item__link article-row-right__tabLinks w-slide__btn details-tab         <div class="relative"><a href="#" data-db-target-for="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865" data-db-switch="icon-close_thin" aria-haspopup="true" aria-controls="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Pop" role="button" id="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Ctrl" aria-label="Tools" class="article-tools__ctrl"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Tools"></i><span>Tools</span></a><div data-db-target-of="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865" aria-labelledby="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Ctrl" id="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Pop" class="article-tools__block fixed dropBlock__holder"><ul role="menu" class="rlist w-slide--list"><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/action/rightsLink?doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200&amp;mode=" role="menuitem" target="_blank"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-permissions-key"></i><span>Request permission</span></a></li><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200" role="menuitem" target="_self"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-export-icon"></i><span>Export citation</span></a></li><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="/personalize/addFavoritePublication?doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200" role="menuitem" target="_self"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-favorites"></i><span>Add to favorites</span></a></li><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="/action/addCitationAlert?doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200" role="menuitem" target="_self"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Track-citations"></i><span>Track citation</span></a></li></ul></div></div>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d55947609" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Metallic-phase iron sulfide (e.g., Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>) is a promising candidate for high power density sodium storage anode due to the inherent metal electronic conductivity and unhindered sodium-ion diffusion kinetics. Nevertheless, long-cycle stability can not be achieved simultaneously while designing a fast-charging Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-based anode. Herein, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> encapsulated in carbon-sulfur bonds doped hollow carbon fibers (NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>) is designed and synthesized for sodium-ion storage. The NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> including metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> embrace higher electron specific conductivity, electrochemical reversibility, and fast sodium-ion diffusion. Moreover, the carbonaceous fibers with polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> exhibit a fixed confinement effect for electrochemical conversion intermediates contributing to long cycle life. In conclusion, combined with theoretical study and experimental analysis, the multinomial optimized NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is demonstrated to integrate a suitable structure for higher capacity, fast charging, and longer cycle life. The full cell shows a power density of 1639.6&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and an energy density of 204.5&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, over 120 long cycles of stability at 1.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The underlying mechanism of metal sulfide structure engineering is revealed by in-depth analysis, which provides constructive guidance for designing the next generation of durable high-power density sodium storage anodes.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202302200-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202302200-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are regarded as the most cost-effective substitute for largescale power storage because sodium exhibits similar electrochemical properties and is far more abundant than lithium (Na: 23.0&nbsp;wt.% vs Li: 0.017&nbsp;wt.%).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0001_R_d55947601e555" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">1</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0004_R_d55947601e555" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - ACS Energy Lett.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hence, SIBs have been extensively researched in both academic circles and the industrial community recently.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0005_R_d55947601e560" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy Environ. Sci.">5</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0007_R_d55947601e560" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Electrochem. Energy Rev.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Excellent rate characteristics and high reversible capacity have been proven for high-power 26650-type columniform SIBs in the early commercialization stage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0008_R_d55947601e565" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Chin. Phys. Lett.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to recent reports, anode and cathode materials with good storage properties of sodium ions have been satisfactorily developed.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0009_R_d55947601e571" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Science">9</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0012_R_d55947601e571" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Electrochem. Energy Rev.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nonetheless, it remains challenging to probe befitting anodes both with matchable fast-charging properties (high power density) and a durable long lifespan for large-volume Na-ion storage and slow sodium-ion diffusion. Of all anode materials for SIBs, the multivalent iron sulfides are a representative progressive in the transition family of metal chalcogenides anodes for fast-charging in SIBs due to its inherent electronic/physiochemical preponderance,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0013_R_d55947601e576" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Mater.">13</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0015_R_d55947601e576" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Energy Storage Mater.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> such as significant theoretical capacity (Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>: 663&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), environmental friendliness and cost-effectiveness.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0016_R_d55947601e588" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0018_R_d55947601e588" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Different from other kinds of iron sulfide phases, the thermodynamically stable metallic phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> has a steerable crystal structure and electronic properties due to its unique polymorphic nature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0019_R_d55947601e599" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem.">19</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0021_R_d55947601e599" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small Methods">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For instance, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> embraces a bandgap energy of ≈0&nbsp;eV like a conductor, but FeS<sub>2</sub> are semiconductors up to 1.72&nbsp;eV, which caused manipulated electronic properties for Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0022_R_d55947601e615" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Energy Storage Mater.">22</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0023_R_d55947601e615" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Mater. Chem. A">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> behaves with metallic properties and significantly enhanced electron conductivity, enabling rapid charge-transfer kinetics, and its octahedral structure with extended layer spacing is more beneficial to accelerating Na-ion diffusion dynamics by reducing the energy barriers of diffusion. Besides, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is proven to have a strong ability to restrain the dissolution of anions in electrochemical conversions on account of their higher bond energies than FeS<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0018_R_d55947601e632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">18</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0019_R_d55947601e632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem.">19</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0024_R_d55947601e632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These combined advantages make the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-based material an attractive fast-charging anode for Na-ion storage.</p>
         
         <p>Nevertheless, these intercalation transition processes based on Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode materials often occur heterogeneous conversion and volume swelling that leads to unsatisfying rate capacity and nondurable cyclic lifespan, especially as a fast-charging anode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0025_R_d55947601e648" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Power Sources">25</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0027_R_d55947601e648" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Energy Environ. Sci.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Until now, many studies have been reported to alleviate the problems mentioned above, such as modification by flexible carbonaceous materials, lower nanoscale structures (0D–3D),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0006_R_d55947601e653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Small">6</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0016_R_d55947601e653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0020_R_d55947601e653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Storage Mater.">20</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0028_R_d55947601e653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">28</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0029_R_d55947601e653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Small">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and optimization of electrolyte constituents.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0027_R_d55947601e659" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Energy Environ. Sci.">27</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0030_R_d55947601e659" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv. Mater. Interfaces">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In electrochemical conversions, compositing with carbonaceous is a common solution to relieve the volume swelling of metal sulfides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0031_R_d55947601e664" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The metal sulfide anodes with high theoretical capacity will be influenced due to the low theoretical capacity of composite amorphous carbonaceous materials and the high mass content.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0020_R_d55947601e670" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Storage Mater.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Otherwise, ether-based electrolytes have been reported could exhibit a satisfactory Na-ion storage performance of metal sulfide anodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0027_R_d55947601e675" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Energy Environ. Sci.">27</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0032_R_d55947601e675" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Ether-based electrolytes include the following advantages: optimizing the components for the formed thinner solid electrolyte interface (SEI) to suppress polysulfide dissolution, excellent electrode wettability, non-flammability, rapid Na-ion diffusion ability, and high electron conductivity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0032_R_d55947601e680" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">32</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0033_R_d55947601e680" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to our previous work,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e686" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> metal sulfide anodes usually suffer from an electrochemical failure while storing sodium in an ester-based system, which seriously affects battery cycle life. The failure exhibited that the rechargeable battery was unable up to the cut-off voltage during the charging period, which in turn led to battery damage and cycle life termination (“under-voltage failure”). Notably, the higher current density accelerated the appearance of “under-voltage failure”. Therefore, a targeted and flexible structural engineering urgently be developed to reach fast-charging and long durable cycle life for Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-based anode along with other hitherto unknown problems. Additionally, the different iron sulfide phase fast storage mechanisms of sodium have not yet been explained, which needs to be further researched.</p>
         
         <p>Therefore, this work designed and composited Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> encapsulated in polar carbon-sulfur bonds doped hollow carbonaceous fibers (NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>) through an adjustable chemical bath sedimentation method followed by different sulfidation processes. NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> have higher electrical conductivity, reversibility of cycling reactions, and Na-ion diffusion advantages combined with an experimental analysis and theoretical calculation, compared with NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. Notably, the hollow carbon fibers with polar carbon-sulfur bonds embrace a powerful function for firm anchoring the dissolved sulfate intermediates, resulting thus the protected active Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles not been destroyed while repeat cycling. Consequently, the multinomial for optimized NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> exhibits attractive electrochemical properties according to a remarkable reversible capacity (642&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles), high initial Coulombic efficiency (≈90%), fast-charging performance (requires over 2000 long cycles stability at 30&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for SIBs), and avoids the“under-voltage failure” issue. Remarkably, the full-cell shows over 120 long cycles stability with a superior power density of 1639.6&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> and an energy density of 204.5&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. In situ, X-ray diffraction patterns and Gibbs reaction energy results revealed that reversible electrochemical phase transitions and low reaction energies promote the fast and durable storage performance of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. The results of adsorption energies, charge density difference, and crystal orbit Hamiltonian population (COHP) revealed that the special polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> exhibited a powerful anchoring effect for electrochemical conversion intermediate product to guarantee the long cycle life of the electrode. The flexible and targeted structure engineering jointly with in-depth fast-charging mechanism analysis put forward guidance for the manufacture of progressive polyvalent metal sulfide materials to establish high-power density SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202302200-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202302200-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>The Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i>-based composites show promising potential application prospects in fast-charging anode materials for SIBs. To explore their Na-ion storage performance, the different phases of Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i> including single Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub>, were first synthesized via a usually molten-salt growth method.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0035_R_d55947601e773" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The X-ray diffraction of two composites analyzed their phase construction (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information), and the peaks present pure Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (JCPDS: 24–0220) and FeS<sub>2</sub>(JCPDS: 42–1340) crystals, respectively. According to our previous work,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e788" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the single metal sulfides always face an abnormal capacity failure which is expressed as “Under-voltage Failure”. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), single Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub> anodes inevitably have this failure as the number of cycles was prolonged, which suggests that the half-cell could not reach the set cut-off voltage in the charging process, and the capacity of charging and discharging is not matched in the early same cycle, and then the battery system is destroyed by the infinite charging failure (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2b,d</a>, Supporting Information). As could be illuminated by the reports on Na-S batteries,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0036_R_d55947601e806" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Chem. Rev.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> we have explored the mechanism of the appearance of this failure that the polysulfide intermediates are not back to metal sulfides but dissolved in electrolyte of dimethyl ether solvent, further convert to a series of copper sulfides and other sulfates via reacts with the Cu current collector. The side reactions between polysulfides and copper ions and the “shuttle effect” both result in the phenomenon of “under-voltage failure”.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e812" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, a carbonaceous skeleton with polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bond doped was designed to be introduced into metal sulfide particles to eliminate the phenomenon of polysulfide intermediates escaping. However, this structural modification could reduce the play of theoretical capacity for metal sulfides, and there is also a need for a more optimized structure to improve the cycle stability under an ultrahigh current density. Thus, Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i> was selected to implement this requirement because of its high electronic conductivity and superior theoretical capacity. Consider on another of our previous works,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0019_R_d55947601e823" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> though FeS<sub>2</sub> has a higher theoretical capacity than Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, the phase of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> has increased intrinsic electronic conductivity, faster Na-ion diffusion, and higher reaction reversibility. Finally, the design Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-based by nanostructured and hybridized with conductive materials could display better electrochemical performance. Therefore, the designed polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds doped hollow carbon fibers (NHCFs-S) were introduced into the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles to assemble the comprehensive structure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. The design synthetic procedure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> for firmly adsorbing the sodium polysulfides in the anode has been illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0001">1a</a>, thus the enhanced durable cycling is guaranteed. NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> has removed the carbon-sulfur bonds in the carbonaceous skeleton by H<sub>2</sub> reduction in the same heat temperature. Initially, the scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3a,b</a> (Supporting Information) revealed the uniform morphology of hollow carbon fiber precursors with ≈150 nanometers in diameter and tens of microns in length, exhibiting a comparative glaze surface. Next, uniform Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>O<i><sub>y</sub></i> nanoparticles were nucleated and grown on the carbon skeleton surface. Then, the crystalline Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>O<i><sub>y</sub></i> is uniformly encapsulated in NHCFs composites (NHCFs-Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>) was achieved via subsequent thermal treatment. In Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4a</a> (Supporting Information), the XRD pattern is a great agreement with the reported Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (JCPDS: 88–0315) and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS: 40–1139) nanocrystals. Considering the equal contents of metal sulfides composites, the percentage of carbonaceous within the precursor NHCFs-Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> is detected by thermogravimetric analysis (TG) and calculated to 35.9&nbsp;wt.%, the result of TG curves as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4b</a> (Supporting Information). The SEM image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0001">1b</a>) exhibits the structure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composite constituted by large number of fine Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles uniformly dispersed on the surface of tubular NHCFs skeleton. The TEM images in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0001">1c,d</a> distinctly shows the homogeneous dispersion of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles with a probably 5–20&nbsp;nm in mean diameter encapsulated in NHCFs composites. The high-resolution TEM images exhibit that encapsulated Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles exist in a uniform carbon layer of ≈0.5–1&nbsp;nm on the surface, attributed to the organic units in the polypyrrole functioning as a source generating a thin layer of carbonaceous on the surface of Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>O<i><sub>y</sub></i> nanoparticles in the thermal treatment.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0035_R_d55947601e948" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0001">1e</a>, the unambiguous crystal lattice fringe spacing is 0.264&nbsp;nm, and it is a good coincidence in the (004) plane of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, demonstrating the properties of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nano-sized particles. As the comparison, the SEM images of NHCFs-Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2,</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> as displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5a–c</a>, shows that different sulfidation and subsequent reduction would not affect the microstructure of the material, expect the evolution of polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in the carbonaceous component. In Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6a–d</a>, the TEM images of NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> show the similar homogeneous dispersion of FeS<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles encapsulated in NHCFs composites. Notably, the unambiguous crystal lattice fringe spacing is 0.270&nbsp;nm, which is a great coincidence in the (200) plane of FeS<sub>2</sub>, indicating the properties of nano-sized particles FeS<sub>2</sub>. Furthermore, the particles of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> assembled and grew even bigger without the carbonaceous skeleton in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7a,b</a> (Supporting Information), proving the vital function of the carbonaceous component in preventing the agglomeration of nano-sized particles. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0001">1f–i</a>, the SEM, TEM images, and the interrelated energy dispersive spectroscopy mapping of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> expressly exhibited the uniform element distribution of carbon, sulfur, and iron. Notably, the S atom uniformly distributes in the carbon skeleton compared with the Fe atom, indicating that the S-doped in carbon component and the existing evidence of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S polar bonds, thus the exceptional performance of the long lifespan is guaranteed. To explore the pore channel architecture, the nitrogen adsorption/desorption isotherms were detected, and the curves were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8a,b</a> (Supporting Information). The NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composites displayed a lower specific surface area of 16.21&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and nearly no pore volume. The small exposed surface could avert the occurrence of undesirable reactions from sodium polysulfides and Cu ions, which could guarantee durable performance while extended cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e1022" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202302200-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e2f16904-e544-4673-9e71-063a32855e20/smll202302200-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e2f16904-e544-4673-9e71-063a32855e20/smll202302200-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/47db4eae-026e-42ce-86fa-1b3afc06fd72/smll202302200-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e2f16904-e544-4673-9e71-063a32855e20/smll202302200-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202302200-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The schematic diagram for the synthetic procedure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composites. b) SEM images of NHCF-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, c–f) TEM images of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> with g–i) the EDX mappings of C, Fe, and S elements.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The phase composition and crystallinity of composited materials were identified via an X-ray diffraction (XRD) test. In <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2a</a>, the diffraction peaks of composites after different sulfidation is in great consistent with the standard XRD pattern of hexagonal crystalline phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (JCPDS: 24–0220) via CS<sub>2</sub> vapor sulfuration, and cubic crystalline phase FeS<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS: 42–1340) by sulfur powder, it indicates that the oxide is completely converted to the different target iron sulfides phase. In particular, the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composites were dismissed at a reduction H<sub>2</sub> atmosphere to synthesize the NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> contrast composite. Similarly, XRD was used to test the phase purity and crystal architecture of NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> without C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds, and all peaks well correspond to the same Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> card (JCPDS: 24–0220 and 29–0723). The Raman spectrum of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> powders in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2b</a> at ≈218, 281, and 390&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, consistent with the <i>E</i><sub>g</sub>, <i>T</i><sub>g</sub> (1) and A<sub>g</sub> modes of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> crystal, respectively compared with NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0025_R_d55947601e1132" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Power Sources">25</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0037_R_d55947601e1132" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> both demonstrating that the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase construction is better preserved for the composite comparison after reduction. In addition, the Raman spectrum further measures the carbonaceous fiber microstructure. Two peaks centered at 1353 and 1564&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> were presented in Raman spectrum in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2b</a>, attributed to amorphous carbon or sp<sup>3</sup> carbon atoms in defects (D band) and ordered graphitic structures of sp<sup>2</sup> C atoms. (G band), respectively. The I<sub>D</sub>/I<sub>G</sub> proportion was calculated to estimate the unordered degree of carbonaceous composites.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0038_R_d55947601e1155" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Nat. Energy">38</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0039_R_d55947601e1155" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nat. Commun.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The value of I<sub>D</sub>/I<sub>G</sub> is fitted and calculated to be 1.02 for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, indicating that well enough conductivity and more polar C-S species affect the surface carbon atoms structure of NHCFs, resulting in anchor active Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and enhance the sodium ion storage performance. Notably, a special weak peak centered at 648&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, corresponds to the ring stretching vibrations of the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds plane bending.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e1182" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0040_R_d55947601e1182" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Energy Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The existence of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S could have a strong absorption for the intermediate products sodium polysulfides during the electrochemical process, contributing to the long cycle stability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202302200-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/beb75407-1eb1-4166-98ac-29d59fa723cd/smll202302200-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/beb75407-1eb1-4166-98ac-29d59fa723cd/smll202302200-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/14aa71ec-77c2-4c20-9705-1972b3f89d57/smll202302200-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/beb75407-1eb1-4166-98ac-29d59fa723cd/smll202302200-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202302200-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The X-ray diffraction patterns from 10–90° with a scan rate of 5&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and b) Raman spectrum of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>. c) Raman spectrum, d) Fourier transforms IR spectra, and e) XPS spectra of NHCF-CS<sub>2</sub>, NHCF-Sulfur, and NHCF-R-CS<sub>2</sub>. f) High-resolution XPS profiles of the S 2p region for NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub>. g) High-resolution XPS profiles of the S 2p region for NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>. h) The proportion of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To distinguish the peculiarity of different polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in different composites, various optical characteristics data were designed and analyzed for calibration. Besides, NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-Sulfur, and NHCFs-R-CS<sub>2</sub> have been produced in a similar way (Scheme&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information) which removed the sulfides to assist in the calibration of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds. The Raman spectrum of NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-Sulfur, and NHCFs-R-CS<sub>2</sub> as exhibited in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2c</a>, two weak peaks near 487 and 650&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> only could be distinguished in NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-Sulfur composites, consistent with the ring stretching and angular vibrations respectively of the short-chain C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds plane bending.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0041_R_d55947601e1276" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0042_R_d55947601e1276" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Adv. Energy Mater.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the FT-IR spectrum of NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-Sulfur in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2d</a> displays the additional weak peaks ≈622, 681, and 874&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, resulting from the different ring stretching and angular vibrations of short-chain C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0040_R_d55947601e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Energy Mater.">40</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0041_R_d55947601e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0043_R_d55947601e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Adv. Energy Mater.">43</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0044_R_d55947601e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - ACS Nano">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, compared with NHCFs-Sulfur and NHCFs-R-CS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> presents a unique peak near 1154&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, which ascribes to the stretching vibrations of CS bonds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e1301" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0045_R_d55947601e1301" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater.">45</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0046_R_d55947601e1301" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Adv. Mater.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The analysis results indicate that NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> include a greater variety of covalent bonds between carbon and sulfur atoms, ensuring the great cycle stability of storage sodium. The valence states of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and detailed interaction between NHCFs-S (various C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds) and Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> were detected by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). The tested full spectra of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> reveal the presence of S, C, O, and Fe atoms, and no other elements were detected in these samples, indicating the purity of materials was verified again (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9a</a>, Supporting Information). This result is similar in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8,</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub> samples. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2e</a>, the peak of S 2p for the full spectra data of NHCFs-R-CS<sub>2</sub> is disappeared compared with NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-Sulfur, confirming the S atom in NHCFs skeleton has been removed. The high-resolution XPS detail spectra of S 2p in the region of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8,</sub> and NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> along with the different fitted peaks were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2f</a>. Compared to Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, two extra peaks located at 162.4 and 161.4&nbsp;eV in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> can be concerned with the characteristic peaks of HS-C and CS bonds, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0045_R_d55947601e1379" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, linked with the disappearance of S 2p for the full spectrum of NHCSs-R-CS<sub>2</sub>, the disappearance of the above two peaks forcefully proved the elimination of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in the carbonaceous fibers of NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. Moreover, there are other peaks at 164.9 and 163.8&nbsp;eV positions in Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, that could be related to the Fe-S 2p<sub>1/2</sub> and Fe-S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles, but those two peaks for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> would be associated with C-S-Fe 2p<sub>1/2</sub> and C-S-Fe 2p<sub>3/2</sub> of the effect of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles with NHCFs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0016_R_d55947601e1425" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0018_R_d55947601e1425" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Similarly, the extra peak of S 2p for the NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> center at 162.6&nbsp;eV in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2g</a>, could be associated with the characteristic peak of HS<span class="icomoon"></span>C bonds. The two peaks at 164.9 and 163.8&nbsp;eV positions of NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> can also be attributed to C-S-Fe 2p<sub>1/2</sub> and C-S-Fe 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, respectively. Finally, the last two peaks approximately at 169.6 and 168.5&nbsp;eV of all composites indicate the presence of SO<sub>4</sub><sup>2−</sup>, which stems from partially oxidized sulfur species on the material surface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0045_R_d55947601e1446" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Whilst, the C 1s spectra in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> could be categorized into three obvious peaks close located at 284.8, 286.1, and 289.1&nbsp;eV, consistent with C<span class="icomoon"></span>C/CC, C<span class="icomoon"></span>S, and O<span class="icomoon"></span>CO bonds, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9b–d</a>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0044_R_d55947601e1463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - ACS Nano">44</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0047_R_d55947601e1463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Nat. Commun.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> demonstrating the existence of the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds between the carbon skeleton and iron sulfide particles. Particularly, the percentage of those three different carbon-based bonds has been calculated by area content in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0002">2h</a>. The results exhibit NHCFS-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFS-CS<sub>2</sub> including more C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds than NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>. Notably, the XPS spectra peak shifting of C1s, S2p, and Fe2p in NHCFS-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> indicated that strong interaction exists C-S-Fe bond of NHCFS-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. The additional Fe 2p spectra of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10a–d</a> (Supporting Information) and the N 1s XPS spectra of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> was shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11a–c</a> (Supporting Information), both analyzed.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0039_R_d55947601e1521" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nat. Commun.">39</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0048_R_d55947601e1521" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Mater.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>In conclusion, the polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds play a key role in limiting the shuttling of sodium polysulfides and maintaining the stability of Fe<i><sub>x</sub></i>S<i><sub>y</sub></i>-based anodes in the Na-ion repeat cycling. Furthermore, the phase of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> can build more diverse polar carbon-sulfur bonds with the carbonaceous skeleton ensuring a more stable electrochemical cycle. The intrinsic electronic conductivity and faster Na-ion diffusion of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> on account of the higher reaction reversibility. Therefore, the elaborate structure design of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> will result in the best improved electrochemical cycle stability of electrodes and storage sodium capacity.</p>
         
         <p>For analyzing the advantages between NHCFs including C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds and metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in Na-ion storage performance, this study selected the reduction composite NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> that do not contain C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> which combined FeS<sub>2</sub> phase with NHCFs including C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds as contrast sample. These crystal structures and phase purity has been detailly studied above. The electrochemical properties of three composites were investigated in a half-cells anode under the voltage range from 0.005 to 3&nbsp;V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3a</a> shows the typical cyclic voltammogram (CV) curves of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode with the first five cycles to demonstrate the mechanism of the sodiation and desodiation reaction. There are five main reduction peaks at near 1.43, 0.86, 0.46, 0.19, and 0.04&nbsp;V in the initial cathodic scan. The peak at 1.43&nbsp;V corresponds with the generation of SEI film.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0020_R_d55947601e1577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Storage Mater.">20</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0049_R_d55947601e1577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The peaks at 0.86, 0.46, and 0.19&nbsp;V were assigned to the formation of Na<sub>2</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> (0.86), Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S (0.46), and NaC<i><sub>x</sub></i> (0.19), respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0016_R_d55947601e1592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0021_R_d55947601e1592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small Methods">21</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0026_R_d55947601e1592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0050_R_d55947601e1592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Nano Res.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The redox peaks ≈0.04&nbsp;V may be caused by the pseudocapacitive adsorption of sodium ions at the electrode interface of the nucleated nanoparticles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0034_R_d55947601e1597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Linked with the anodic scan of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12b</a>, Supporting Information), the three oxidation peaks are concentrated at 1.34, 1.54, and 2.12&nbsp;V could be clearly seen in the discharge stage, attribute to the conversion of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase. This evolution could be attributed to the generation of Na<sub>2</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub>2-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub>, and Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0019_R_d55947601e1634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem.">19</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0020_R_d55947601e1634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Storage Mater.">20</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0026_R_d55947601e1634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0049_R_d55947601e1634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the subsequent scan, the oxidation peaks repeat well, and shows great reversibility. Compared with NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-R-CS<sub>2</sub> in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12b,d</a> (Supporting Information), the unique less obvious peaks appearance at 1.77&nbsp;V (reduction peak) and 1.80&nbsp;V (oxidation peak) in the CV curves are ascribed to the formation and fracture of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe and C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in the special structure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12a</a>, Supporting Information) and NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12c</a>, Supporting Information). The nearly overlapped CV curves indicate the dependable reversibility and stability of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> after the first cycle.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202302200-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/39b0e8ee-5ec9-453e-833e-d99b055c6153/smll202302200-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/39b0e8ee-5ec9-453e-833e-d99b055c6153/smll202302200-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/d3779dc6-b85b-4d0f-a4a1-dfa6e0cb0d39/smll202302200-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/39b0e8ee-5ec9-453e-833e-d99b055c6153/smll202302200-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
