                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance for sodium ion batteries: a) cyclic voltammograms of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> at 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> b) cycling performance at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, c) initial Coulombic efficiency, d) rate performance of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. e,f) Nyquist plots of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> before cycling and the relevant linear fits in the low-frequency area. g) CV results of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> at different scan rates from 0.2 to 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1.</sup> h) The determined <i>b</i>-value for the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> was calculated by means of the relationship between peak current and scan rate. i) Normalized contribution ratios of capacitance and diffusion of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> at different scan rates.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The cycle performance of the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anodes are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3b</a> at a current density of 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The designed NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode demonstrates the highest reversible capacity of 642&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles, and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> as the comparison has provided a reversible capacity of 476 and 285&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The increased capacity of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> may be originated from the contribution of pseudocapacitive sodium ion storage. Second, the defects-repairing induced carbon-matrix distributed Mental-S<span class="icomoon"></span>C bonds on the surface play as numerous catalytic centers, promoting the formation of a complete SEI that is conducive to the maintenance of stable high capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0018_R_d55947601e1774" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Thirdly, the synergistic effect of hexagonal facets Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and S-doped carbon skeleton also can improve the capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0026_R_d55947601e1783" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0051_R_d55947601e1783" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Small">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Otherwise, the electrochemically reduced metallic phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles can store a large number of spin-polarized electrons, which results in a large excess capacity and a pronounced change in the interface magnetization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0052_R_d55947601e1793" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Nat. Mater.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Based on the above reasons and combined with the special internal Fe-S-C structure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, the capacity increased obviously. In comparison, the NHCFs-Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> anode has unsatisfying reversible capacities of 238&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with the same test situation in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13a</a> (Supporting Information), and the relevant galvanostatic current discharge/charge curves are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13b</a> (Supporting Information). This result reveals the significant role of the carbonaceous skeleton and sulfides in the high reversible capacities of SIBs. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3c</a>, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anodes exhibit a high initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of ≈89% at the different current densities versus just 82% and 77% in NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, respectively. The corresponding initial galvanostatic current discharge and charge profiles at the current density of 0.2, 1.0, and 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14a–c</a> (Supporting Information), respectively. The initial CV curve of NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8,</sub> and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anodes are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15a</a> (Supporting Information) to explore the reason for high ICE for the special structure of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. They show different reduction potentials of −1.43, −1.12, and −0.86&nbsp;eV, corresponding to NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. The underlying analyses are provided in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15b,c</a> (Supporting Information). The Fermi level of diglyme (DME) reduction (≈−0.13&nbsp;eV) is larger than the anode potential of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (≈−1.43&nbsp;eV) compared with NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> (≈−1.12&nbsp;eV) NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (≈−0.86&nbsp;eV), which could prevent the transfer of electrons from NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> to DME, causing negligible side effects between electrolyte and anodes, and thus higher ICE.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0032_R_d55947601e1889" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">32</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0053_R_d55947601e1889" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - J. Mater. Chem. A">53</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0054_R_d55947601e1889" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Energy Environ. Sci.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anodes also performed great rate capability which was assessed when the current density increased from 0.2 to 20.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and the results are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3d</a>. The NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode showed a relatively durable response at all the current densities studied. As rate performance analysis, specific capacities of 659, 655, 638, 612, 554, and 493&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> are reached for the corresponding specific current densities of 0.2, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, severally. Though at the uppermost current density of 20.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, a high specific capacity of 453&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is gained, showing ≈69% of the capacity retention when the current density up from 0.2 to 20.0&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Additionally, the charge/discharge plateaus for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> maintain great with the smallest polarization at different rates in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a</a> (Supporting Information). In contrast, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> show an obviously lower rate performance with only 345 and 212&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> acquired at 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16b,c</a> (Supporting Information) displayed the galvanostatic current discharge/charge curves. The above results are undoubtedly beneficial because Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> has a good ability to restrain anion release due to the higher bond energies of Fe-S in octahedral structure and the firmly fixed function of the polar carbon-sulfur bonds for the dissolved polysulfide ions. Otherwise, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> exhibit higher powder electronic conductivity compared with other composites in this study (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information), resulting in obtaining a higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient for the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode. These are conducive to the improved cycling stability with a high capacity of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode.</p>
         
         <p>To gain a deeper comprehension about the diffusion kinetics behaviors, the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes were tested via electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) in a frequency range of 200&nbsp;kHz to 100&nbsp;mHz fresh and after 10 cycles. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a</a> (Supporting Information) and Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3e</a> reflected the Nyquist plots before and after cycling for three electrodes, which are made up of a compressed semicircle in the high-frequency area with an oblique line on the low-frequency side.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0018_R_d55947601e1983" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">18</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0023_R_d55947601e1983" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Mater. Chem. A">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The charge transfer resistance (R<i><sub>ct</sub></i>, which was gained from the diameter of the semicircle in the high-medium frequency area) of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is smaller than those of NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>. The R<i><sub>ct</sub></i> values NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> were fitted to be 2.46, 5.30, and 8.00&nbsp;Ω before cycle and 0.39, 0.62, and 1.12&nbsp;Ω after 10 cycles, respectively. Furthermore, the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode with various bond structures exhibits the maximum slope in the Warburg area in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3f</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b</a> (Supporting Information), demonstrating a fast solid-state ion diffusion in the active component.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0031_R_d55947601e2027" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0055_R_d55947601e2027" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Chem. Rev.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Afterwards, the Na-ion diffusion coefficients in cell system were calculated (see Supporting Information for detail) and the results were listed in Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information)). Obviously, the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode exhibits the biggest ion diffusion coefficient of 2.16&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−13</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in comparison with the NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and (4.85&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−14</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (4.31&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−14</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>). This consequence indicates that the existence of the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase and polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> could greatly expedite the Na-ion migration in the dense active part. The electrochemical reaction mechanism and kinetics are further researched through the CV curves at a range of scan rates from 0.2 to 10.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3g</a>. Notably, the peak O1 (1.34) is also linked with the conversion of Fe with C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bond to C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds. The shifts of peaks O1 to a low potential as the scan rate increases indicated the powerful anchoring effect of polar bonding for the reversible conversion while fast-charging state for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. Generally, the b value responds to the charge transfer mechanism (the detailed analysis is shown in Supporting Information). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3h</a>, the <i>b</i> values calculated by the log(<i>i</i>) versus log(<i>v</i>) plots for reduction peaks (R<sub>1</sub>, R<sub>2</sub>, and R<sub>3</sub>) and oxidation peaks (O<sub>1</sub>, O<sub>2</sub>, and O<sub>2</sub>) are 0.88, 1.02, 0.99, 0.91, 0.93, and 0.98, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0056_R_d55947601e2107" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">56</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0057_R_d55947601e2107" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Nat. Mater.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The <i>b</i> value on the verge of 1 indicates the e<sup>−</sup> transfer in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composites is mainly dominated by the interfacial capacitive behavior, which will guarantee fast Na-ion storage kinetics. In comparison, the <i>b</i> values of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> are higher than NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and NHCFs-CS<sub>2</sub>, (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19a–f</a>, Supporting Information), further revealing the preponderance structure design of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> active substance and polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in the carbonaceous fibers on increasing ion diffusion rate in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrodes. To quantitatively investigate the contribution of each course, the current <i>i</i> at a stationary potential <i>V</i> was set equal to diffusion-controlled reactions and capacitive behaviors as follows: <i>i</i> (<i>V</i>)&nbsp;=&nbsp;<i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v+k</i><sub>2</sub>ν<sup>1/2</sup>. As the proportion of current increases through Na-ion diffusion, capacitive processes could be distinguished by calculating the <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> constants.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0056_R_d55947601e2171" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">56</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0057_R_d55947601e2171" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Nat. Mater.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The pseudocapacitance contributions of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>, and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20a,c,e</a>, Supporting Information) are 84%, 83%, and 78% at 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, and the typical voltage profile for calculated pseudocapacitive current associated with the measured current is also displayed. Moreover, the capacitive involvement of the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode was expanded to 93% at 5.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0003">3i</a>) as the scan rates increased. The NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> were analyzed by the same procedure (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20b,d</a>, Supporting Information). Notably, the contribution of the capacitive process for NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> was smaller than that of the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> at all scan rates. It is indubitable that the higher percentage of the pseudocapacitive contribution could promote faster Na-ion transmission, reinforcing the rate capability of the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, which benefit from the conductive Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase and active C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds structure.</p>
         
         <p>As shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4</a>, the mechanism of fast and long lifespan cyclic stability of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode was further analyzed to confirm the structural viability protected by the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds in the carbonaceous carrier. The three initial structures of single-layer graphene contain C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds with Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and FeS<sub>2</sub>(200), and single-layer graphene without C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds but with Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) was built in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information), named as G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004), G-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(004) and G-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) respectively. The three stabilized structures are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4a</a>, the single-layer graphene with C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds tended to bond with Fe and S atoms in the phase of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub>. However, the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase could bond with graphene layer while removing the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bond in carbon skeleton. Lined with the experimental data described above, the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> composites contain a unique bonding structure of C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe. In order to distinguish the difference in the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonding of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub> phases, The charge density difference of G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and G-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200) was calculated and the results displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4b</a>, the G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) exhibit more flexible and stable bonding structure, and the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe charge of G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in the bonding and electron coupling process moves faster and exist more bonding polarization direction, compare with G-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200). This result revealed that the existence of special C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode ensures a high degree of flexibility and reversibility in the electrochemical conversion process of bonding structure, as well as rapid promotion of sodium ion diffusion.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0047_R_d55947601e2320" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Nat. Commun.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bond strength can be evaluated by the integration crystal orbit Hamiltonian population (-ICOHP) value. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4c,d</a>, the -ICOHP values of Fe<span class="icomoon"></span>S and C<span class="icomoon"></span>S bonds in C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds of G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) is 3.42 and 7.12 respectively, which both higher than G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) only 2.88 and 6.05 respectively. Thus, after strong C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe hybridization, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode with special C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds could immobilize the electrochemical conversion products more permanently, promoting cycle stability during discharge. Furthermore, the strong adsorption ability of the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bond structure in carbon skeleton for Na<sub>2</sub>S<i><sub>x</sub></i> (our previous work has proven that <i>x</i>&nbsp;≤&nbsp;4) was calculated in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a> (Supporting Information) and Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4e</a>. The schematic diagram of the adsorption energy calculation and stable crystal structure of G-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and G-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200) containing C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds and G-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) adsorbing Na<sub>2</sub>S, Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>2</sub>, and Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> was Statistics in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4e</a>. The calculated adsorption energy values of Graphene-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) with Na<sub>2</sub>S, Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> are all higher than G-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200) and G-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004). This result explains that the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonding in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> embraces a powerful adsorption behavior on Na<sub>2</sub>S<i><sub>x</sub></i> species, thus avoiding the shuttling of Na<sub>2</sub>S<i><sub>x</sub></i> in the electrochemical conversion processes and further effectively preventing their side reactions. This result reflects that the long durable cycle life was guaranteed by the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe banding structure in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode, which plays a protective effect for active metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202302200-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/244d9017-66cc-4be1-883c-fca7561342f4/smll202302200-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/244d9017-66cc-4be1-883c-fca7561342f4/smll202302200-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/385b4205-7af7-48d7-b46c-2eedd26b0b64/smll202302200-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/244d9017-66cc-4be1-883c-fca7561342f4/smll202302200-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">

                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Stable bonding structure diagram of S-doped monolayer graphene with Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and FeS<sub>2</sub>(200), and monolayer graphene with Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004). b) The charge density difference of Graphene-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and Graphene-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200). Yellow and blue areas represent increased and decreased electron density, respectively. c) The crystal orbit Hamiltonian population of Fe-S and C-S for Graphene-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and Graphene-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200), d) the corresponding -ICOHP value of these bonds. e) Calculated adsorption energies of Na<sub>2</sub>S, Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> with Graphene-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>(004) and Graphene-S-FeS<sub>2</sub>(200). Brown, orange, yellow, and blue balls represent carbon, iron, sulfur, and sodium atoms, respectively. f) Long lifespan of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> at a range of high current density from 2.0 to 30.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. g) Statistical scatter graph about the cycle life of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub>-based anodes in this study under diverse high current densities.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The experimental results also well verify the theoretical calculation results above. As the cycle number extends to 2000 for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode at the high current density of 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the sodium storage capacity is still maintained at 545&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4f</a>) with the Coulombic efficiency close to 100%. Furthermore, the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode keeps the high capacity of 515, 376, and 268&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after cycling 2000 times at the higher current densities 5.0, 10.0, and 30.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. After 2000 cycles, the capacity retention ratio of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> reaches ≈80% (based on the 200<sup>th</sup> capacity) even under an extremely high current density of 30.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. In comparison, the NHCFs-S-FeS<sub>2</sub> and NHCFs-R-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anodes have nondurable cycle performance under the high current density condition. The detailed results of cycle life for different anodes in this study are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0004">4g</a> and Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information), the corresponding analysis is displayed in Supporting Information. In conclusion, the metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> ensures a high reversible capacity and Na-ion diffusion, and C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds functioned a durable long cycle life. Comprehensively, the integration of effective carbonaceous components and high-active Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles of the well-designed NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> structure could result in high Na-ion storage capacity and durable long-cycle property.</p>
         
         <p>The mechanism of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode including a special C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bond for its electrochemical long cycle life has been displayed above. Otherwise, there explores the superior properties of active metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode contribute to the super high reversible capacity and rate performance in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5</a>. The in situ XRD was carried out to further study the sodium storage mechanism of the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5a</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information). Obviously, the densities of three peaks of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> near 29.9°, 33.9°, and 43.8°, and the intensity of the three peaks gradually diminishes during the 3rd discharge process, which means the main phase of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> had involved in the sodiation reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0016_R_d55947601e2602" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Observably, the two peaks at 29.9° and 43.8° tend to lower angles in the sodiation and recover to their original angles in the desodiation. This verifies the contraction of partial sodiation product Na<sub>3</sub>(FeS<sub>2</sub>)<sub>2</sub> and small lattice spacing expansion, resulting from the sodium ions insertion/extraction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0021_R_d55947601e2613" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small Methods">21</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0026_R_d55947601e2613" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the products of transformation reaction, three peaks disappeared while discharge to lower potential, and the peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>S (38.7°) and Fe (41.3°) gradually appeared during the discharge process and continued to exist in the subsequent process. This demonstrates that Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is continuously converted into Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S during the sodium storage process in the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0049_R_d55947601e2632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">49</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0050_R_d55947601e2632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Nano Res.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, three peaks 29.9°, 33.9°, and 43.8° of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> turn back to their original position in the charge condition, manifesting that the reaction might return to the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase. Moreover, in hexagonal Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> the Fe atom layer in hexagonal Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is sandwiched between S layers with a trigonal prismatic coordination of Fe atom. The hexagonal phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> owns a honeycomb-like lattice with minor variation in intensity contrast between two adjacent sites while the charge-discharge process, enhanced the stability of the active Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0026_R_d55947601e2663" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0051_R_d55947601e2663" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Small">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These discoveries elucidated the intercalation reaction mechanism of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> during the cycling process. Considering the previous analysis of the CV curves and differential capacity curves, the relevant schematic diagram of the sodium storage mechanism describes the intercalation reaction along with the conversion reaction mechanisms of the metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, which schemed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5b</a> corresponds to the following equations.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202302200-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6419ab66-3649-4900-8ed2-3415c74c69f1/smll202302200-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>

                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The sodium storage mechanism of metallic-phase NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. a) In situ XRD characterization of the sodium storage mechanism of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> for the 3rd cycle. b) Schematic diagram of sodium storage mechanism of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, describing intercalation reaction combined with transformation reaction. c) Statistical scatter figure about the cycle capacity of anodes in this study at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. d) The Gibb free energy of one electron transfer of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub> reaction with sodium ion. e) The comparison of rate properties for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> with recently reported high-performance Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-based SIBs anodes. f) The comparison of cycling performance of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> with recently reported fast-charging ferric sulfide-based SIBs anodes.</div>

         </section>

                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\[
\begin{array}{*{20}{c}}{4N{a_{2 - {\rm{x}}}}Fe{S_2} + 3Fe \to F{e_7}{{\rm{S}}_8} + (8 - 4{\rm{x}}){{\rm{e}}^ - } + (8 - 4{\rm{x}})Na}\end{array}

                     </semantics>
                     </math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>To verify the self-buffering effect of active particles on cycling stability, postmortem SEM images of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> after different numbers of cycles were compared and analyzed (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information). After Na-ion insertion/extraction in the first cycle (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27b</a>, Supporting Information), NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> nearly returned to its original structure without any cracks, and the surface of the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particle became smooth with countless particles covering it, which ascribed to the formation of SEI film. After 1000 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27c,d</a>, Supporting Information), the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> still maintain an integrity structure indicating that the designed NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> structure has high reversible sodium storage performance. Nevertheless, the iron sulfide particles become smoother with the cycles which attribute to the complex phase transition. Based on these superior properties of metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, fast and durable sodium-ion storage of the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode could be achieved by the assisted structure engineering. Three compounds with different Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> contents were synthesized to evaluate the influence of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> proportion in the designed structure, named NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-Max, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8,</sub> and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-Few. The Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> components were successfully composited into the hybrids as revealed by the XRD results in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28a</a> (Supporting Information). Thermogravimetric curves revealed the contents of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> are 24%, 54%, and 75% (wt.%) for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-Max, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8,</sub> and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-Few, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28b</a>, calculation details are listed in Supporting Information). As shown in statistical Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5c</a>, the NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-Max, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and FeS<sub>2</sub> exhibit superior Na-ion storage capacity than pure Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, nearly reached the theoretic capacity under the current density of 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. However, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-Max also appeared unendurable cycle performance, which failed in the 189<sup>th</sup> cycle at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28c,d</a>, Supporting Information). This result is attributed to the unstable structure integrity because of an excessive amount of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, which can be verified by the SEM and TEM images in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a> (Supporting Information).</div>
         
         <p>To gain insight into the above experimental results, as listed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a> (Supporting Information), the Gibbs free energy variation of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, FeS<sub>2,</sub> and other crystal cells was calculated in these reactions of this study first. The Gibbs free energy changes of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub> reacting with one Na-ion were simulated to reflect the electrochemical reaction reversibility in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5d</a>. Consequently, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is in possession of even higher sodiation/desodiation reversibility than the phase of FeS<sub>2</sub> because of the higher neutral number of Gibbs free energy changes (−1.2332&nbsp;eV for Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and −1.2397&nbsp;eV for FeS<sub>2</sub>). Compared with the FeS<sub>2</sub> anode, sodium ion has higher reaction reversibility, thus ensuring better reversible capacity. The band energy and density of states (DOS) have been mapped and analyzed by Python Materials Genomics (pymatgen) in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a> (Supporting Information). The metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> embraces a bandgap of ≈0&nbsp;eV while that of FeS<sub>2</sub> is up to 1.72&nbsp;eV. Otherwise, the contrast of the rate capability in storage sodium properties with reported research on Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-based anodes is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5e</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), proving that the excellent rate capability and durable long cycle at high current density designed NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composite structure concerning the most of reported works.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0020_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Storage Mater.">20</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0021_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small Methods">21</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0025_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Power Sources">25</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0026_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0037_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">37</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0049_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">49</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0050_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Nano Res.">50</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0058_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - J. Mater. Chem. A">58</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0060_R_d55947601e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Nanoscale">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Considering on the performance of sodium storage according to long-term cyclicity and rate capability, NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> electrode is superior to numerous recently reported ferric sulfides anodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0005">5f</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202302200-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0017_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Energy Environ. Sci.">17</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0018_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">18</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0020_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Storage Mater.">20</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0021_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Small Methods">21</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0025_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Power Sources">25</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0027_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Energy Environ. Sci.">27</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0037_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">37</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0049_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">49</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0050_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Nano Res.">50</a>, <a href="#smll202302200-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0058_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - J. Mater. Chem. A">58</a>-<a href="#smll202302200-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202302200-bib-0069_R_d55947601e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - J. Mater. Chem. A">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The above results suggest the effectiveness of the C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds doped hollow carbon fibers in the anchoring of active metallic Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles, ensuring the fast and durable theoretical capacity of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> achieved. This provides a possibility for the design of a stable and fast sodium storage anode with a high specific capacity.</p>
         
         <p>Based on the above-explored mechanisms, the structure functions of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode were schemed in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0006">6a</a>, including special C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bond for its electrochemical durability and long cycle life and metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> contribute to its high reversible capacity and fast Na-ion diffusion. To further evaluate the fast-charge application of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> as SIBs anode, the full-cells were developed via employing the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/carbon as cathode (The SEM images of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/carbon are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a>, Supporting Information) and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> as anode. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0006">6b,c</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33</a> (Supporting Information), the half-cell of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/carbon and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode exhibited charge/discharge profiles/peaks with a distinctive plateau at ≈3.4 and 1.4&nbsp;V, respectively. The large work potential difference indicated the improved electrochemical kinetics. The full cells were processed under constant current (CC) mode for charging and discharging. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0006">6d</a>, the full-cell delivered the durable charge/discharge capacities of 92.7/92.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 110&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 160 cycles. Moreover, it presented superior fast-charging performances with a high discharge capacity of 77.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at a high current density of 1.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with capacity retention of 89% after 120 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0006">6f</a>), demonstrating excellent cycling stability. Notably, the full-cell delivered a power density of 1639.6&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and an energy density of 204.5&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, according to the details in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a> (Supporting Information). With the fast-charging performance of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode-based full-cell, a pouch full-cell was assembled successfully in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202302200-fig-0006">6e</a> to power the light-emitting diode, verifying its great promise in fast-charging SIBs for practical application.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202302200-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3b1baafc-39f1-4b9f-b928-4d6e736a84df/smll202302200-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3b1baafc-39f1-4b9f-b928-4d6e736a84df/smll202302200-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c4653cc2-2b86-4708-ad4e-006917c03b3c/smll202302200-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3b1baafc-39f1-4b9f-b928-4d6e736a84df/smll202302200-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202302200-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302200" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The functions of every structure design for NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> to achieve great fast-charging and long cycle life. b–f) Electrochemical performances of the as-prepared full-cell based on the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/carbon cathode and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode. b) CV curves and c) typical charge-discharge profiles of a half-cell of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/carbon at 1&nbsp;C (1&nbsp;C&nbsp;=&nbsp;110&nbsp;mA g<sub>Na3V2(PO4)3/carbon</sub><sup>−1</sup>) and NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. d) Cycling performances of the full-cell along with the CEs at 110&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. e) Optical images of the LED powered by pouch full-cell. f) Fast and durable cycling performances of the full-cell along with the CEs at 1100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The n/p ratio of all full-cell was set to 1.1.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202302200-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202302200-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>In conclusion, this work designed and synthesized NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> composites as a high power density SIBs anode that Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> was encapsulated in C-S bonds containing hollow carbon fibers. The metallic-phase Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> ensured a high reversible capacity and fast Na-ion diffusion kinetics, and C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds functioned a durable long cycle life. Consequently, the optimized NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> anode for SIBs appears fascinating electrochemical performance according to excellent reversible capacity (642&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles), high initial Coulombic efficiency (≈90%), remarkable rate performance, and impressive long cycling stability. (2000 cycles under a high current density of 30&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) The full-cell shows over 120 long cycles stability with a power density of 1639.6&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and an energy density of 204.5&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Experimental investigation and theoretical analysis collectively revealed the reversible electrochemical phase transitions and low reaction energies barriers that promoted the fast electrochemical reaction, and the doped polar C<span class="icomoon"></span>S<span class="icomoon"></span>Fe bonds guaranteed the long durable cycle life of NHCFs-S-Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>. This targeted and flexible structure engineering jointly with in-depth under-voltage failure mechanism exploration provides a guidance for the manufacture of advanced polyvalent metal sulfides-based anode to realize high power density and long-cycling energy storage systems.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
